AstraForge is organized into these major layers:

1. **Workspace layer** — projects, notebooks, models, experiments, assets, documents, and dashboards
2. **Computation layer** — numerical solvers, simulation engines, GPU/HPC dispatch, workflow execution
3. **Data layer** — ingestion, normalization, time series, files, metadata, provenance, cataloging
4. **Modeling layer** — equations, schemas, simulations, digital twins, graph models, semantic models
5. **Collaboration layer** — reviews, comments, tasks, versioning, approvals, provenance trails
6. **Governance layer** — security, compliance, validation, auditability, policy enforcement
7. **Integration layer** — APIs, SDKs, connectors, instrumentation, enterprise systems, cloud services
8. **Intelligence layer** — AI copilots, anomaly detection, automated insights, report generation

---

# 3) Core platform features

## 3.1 Unified project workspace

* Multi-project and multi-tenant workspaces
* Hierarchical project structures
* Nested folders, tags, labels, and metadata
* Cross-project linking

# 24) What makes it “comprehensive”

The platform is comprehensive because it covers the full lifecycle:

**idea → hypothesis → model → data → simulation → experiment → validation → report → deployment → monitoring → improvement**

That means it is not just a simulation tool, not just a lab notebook, not just a dashboard system, and not just an enterprise data platform. It is all of those, connected by traceability, governance, and reusable infrastructure.

---

# 25) One-sentence description

**AstraForge is a universal scientific and engineering operating environment that unifies modeling, simulation, experimentation, data, collaboration, AI assistance, compliance, and deployment in one traceable platform.**

If you want, I can turn this into a formal product specification, a software architecture diagram in text, or a feature matrix by user role.


Below is a clean modular decomposition of **AstraForge** into platform modules, submodules, and optional domain packs.

# Dependency order

A practical build order would be:

**Foundation → Workspace → Data → Computation → Modeling → Simulation → Experiment → Visualization → Collaboration → AI → Governance → Integration → Deployment → Domain packs**

That structure keeps the platform clean: the base services are stable, the scientific and engineering capabilities are modular, and the domain-specific features remain optional overlays rather than hard dependencies.

I can turn this into a **module map diagram**, a **microservice decomposition**, or a **product roadmap by release phase**.



Below is a practical microservice decomposition for **AstraForge**. It is organized by bounded context, with each service owning its own data and exposing APIs plus domain events.

## 1) Edge and platform entry services

### 1. API Gateway

Front door for all clients.

* Routing, rate limiting, auth propagation, request shaping
* Protocol translation for web, mobile, CLI, and external integrations
* TLS termination, API versioning, throttling

### 2. Identity Service

Authentication and identity lifecycle.

* SSO, MFA, user sessions, service accounts
* OAuth/OIDC/SAML integration
* Token issuance and validation

### 3. Tenant Service

Multi-tenancy and org structure.

* Tenants, organizations, departments, workspaces
* Tenant isolation rules
* Environment scoping: dev/test/prod/air-gapped

### 4. Policy Service

Centralized authorization and policy evaluation.

* RBAC, ABAC, row/field-level policy checks
* Policy-as-code evaluation
* Access decision API for all services

### 5. Audit Service

Immutable security and compliance trail.

* Log all sensitive actions and approvals
* Tamper-evident audit events
* Exportable audit packets

### 6. Notification Service

Cross-channel messaging.

* Email, chat, SMS, in-app notifications
* Alert routing and subscription rules
* Delivery tracking and retries

### 7. Feature Flag Service

Controlled rollout and experiment gating.

* Feature toggles
* Tenant/project/user targeting
* Progressive rollout support

---

## 2) Workspace and collaboration services

### 8. Workspace Service

User-facing container for work.

* Workspaces, project hierarchies, navigation
* Project templates and landing pages
* Workspace membership and visibility

### 9. Asset Catalog Service

Registry for all platform objects.

* Models, datasets, documents, experiments, dashboards, reports
* Global identifiers, tags, labels, metadata
* Object ownership and lifecycle state

### 10. Document Service

Technical document management.

* Specs, SOPs, design docs, lab notes, validation records
* Rich text, attachments, comments
* Document versioning and approvals

### 11. Collaboration Service

Team interaction around artifacts.

* Comments, mentions, tasks, review threads
* Shared annotations on models, datasets, charts, and reports
* Decision logs and discussion history

### 12. Search Service

Unified search across the platform.

* Full-text search
* Semantic search
* Filters, facets, and saved queries
* Indexes assets, documents, experiments, datasets, and events

### 13. Knowledge Graph Service

Semantic knowledge representation.

* Ontologies, concepts, entity relationships
* Provenance links and dependency graphs
* Graph queries for traceability and discovery

## 3) Data platform services

### 14. Ingestion Service

# Recommended communication model

Use a mostly event-driven architecture:

* **Synchronous APIs** for commands and reads: REST/gRPC/GraphQL
* **Asynchronous events** for state changes: Kafka, NATS, or equivalent
* **Outbox pattern** in every service for reliable event publication
* **Saga orchestration** for multi-service workflows such as experiment execution, report generation, or release approval

Typical events:

* `AssetCreated`
* `DatasetCertified`
* `ModelReleased`
* `ExperimentRunStarted`
* `SimulationCompleted`
* `CalibrationUpdated`
* `TwinDriftDetected`
* `RequirementChanged`
* `ReportPublished`
* `AccessRevoked`

---

# Storage assignment by service

Keep storage private to each service:

* **PostgreSQL**: identity metadata, workspace metadata, model registry, experiments, requirements, approvals
* **Time-series store**: telemetry, measurements, alarms
* **Object storage**: artifacts, reports, binaries, simulation outputs
* **Graph store**: knowledge graph, provenance, dependency queries
* **Search index**: global search and faceted retrieval
* **Redis/cache**: sessions, short-lived execution state, rate limiting
* **Queue/stream**: orchestration and event propagation

---

# A sensible first implementation slice

If you want the platform to be buildable in phases, start with these services:

1. Identity Service
2. Tenant Service
3. Workspace Service
4. Asset Catalog Service
5. Document Service
6. Ingestion Service
7. Transformation Service
8. Workflow Orchestrator Service
9. Execution Runner Service
10. Model Registry Service
11. Experiment Service
12. Visualization Service
13. Report Composer Service
14. Audit Service
15. Notification Service

That gives you a usable core without over-fragmenting the platform too early.

---

# Service boundary principle

A useful rule is:

* **One service = one business capability**
* **One service = one data ownership boundary**
* **Cross-service joins happen through APIs, projections, or events, not shared databases**

Compact way to think about both
Scientific computing platforms = notation + execution + data + models + experiment control + provenance + publication.
Engineering lifecycle platforms = requirements + models + verification + configuration + safety + traceability + production + operations.
The deeper pattern is that both categories are converging on the same future shape:
real-time and event-driven
API-first and machine-addressable
reproducible by default
provenance-aware
simulation-linked
collaboration-native
governed and auditable
interoperable across tools and institutions



Below is a unified “future software civilization” taxonomy that merges:
open finance / economic infrastructure
scientific computing platforms
engineering lifecycle platforms
into one coherent stack of digital civilization infrastructure.
The organizing principle is:
Reality → Knowledge → Design → Experiment → Production → Economy → Governance → Operations

The underlying pattern
All future software ecosystems are built from a few recurring primitives:
Identity
who is acting
Data
what information exists
Models
how systems behave
Simulation
what could happen
Execution
running real-world operations
Coordination
people and machines working together
Governance
ensuring rules are followed
Economics
allocating resources

The deepest insight
The categories you asked about are actually three layers of one system:
Layer
Role
scientific computing
discover knowledge
engineering lifecycle
build systems
financial/economic infrastructure
allocate resources

Together they form the digital operating system for civilization.

If you'd like, I can also show you something interesting:
the 25–40 core platform types that will likely dominate the global software ecosystem over the next 30 years (the equivalent of the OS / database / cloud platforms of the past).

17) Financial and economic infrastructure software
Below is the full stack I would expect to exist in a far-future open banking / open finance / open data / open everything ecosystem. I am treating it as an interoperable economic operating system, not just a bank-API layer. # Outline — “OmniEng”: A Unified, End-to-End Engineering Platform

Below is a pragmatic, end-to-end outline for architecting, governing, and delivering a massive, multi-domain engineering platform—think Atlassian + SAP + Siemens, but purpose-built for engineering across mechanical, electrical, software, systems, civil, chemical, and process domains.

---

Here’s a fully fleshed-out “Vision & Scope” for the OmniEng platform. I’ve kept it practical: each statement ties to measurable outcomes, operating principles, scope boundaries, and concrete acceptance criteria.

# 1) Vision

**North-star statement**
Create a single, governed **Digital Thread** connecting idea → requirements → architecture/design → simulation → verification/validation → manufacturing/operations → service, across all engineering disciplines and suppliers—so that every decision, artifact, and change is traceable, testable, and operable.

**What the Digital Thread means (concretely)**

* **Continuity of identity:** Every lifecycle artifact (need, requirement, function, design item, part, test, simulation, NC/CAPA, work instruction, asset, field event) has a stable, global ID and version.
* **Typed links + semantics:** Links aren’t just URLs; they’re typed relations (e.g., *satisfies*, *verifies*, *implements*, *causes*, *affects variant X*, *is derived from*) with direction, timestamps, and provenance.
* **Immutable baselines:** Cryptographically signed snapshots of configurations (requirements sets, EBOM/MBOM, software releases) – repeatable builds and audits.
* **Executable models:** MBSE and engineering models are first-class; simulations/analyses are runnable with captured inputs, toolchains, parameters, and seeds for reproducibility.
* **Closed-loop with operations:** Field/plant telemetry, quality signals, and service events feed back into requirements and design decisions through governed change.
* **Multi-tenant + IP boundaries:** Collaboration with suppliers via scoped projects, policy-based access (ABAC), and contract-bound data exchanges.

**Vision acceptance criteria**

* A single artifact graph query can show *why* a design exists (originating needs), *what* verifies it (tests/sim), *where* it’s built (MBOM/work centers), and *how* it’s performing in the field (telemetry/NCs).
* Any released configuration is reconstructible: “build the exact as-shipped system from baseline X, including software, parameters, and calibration artifacts.”
* Compliance evidence packs can be generated on-demand from live data—no manual re-assembly.

---

# 2) Strategic Outcomes → Measurable Objectives

## 2.1 Shorten concept-to-production & reduce rework

* **Objectives (12–18 months):**

  * ↓ **Change lead time** (ECR → ECO) by **35%**.
  * ↓ **Requirements churn-related defects** entering verification by **30%**.
  * ↓ **Prototype cycles** to first article by **25%**.
* **Levers:**

  * Early validation via model-in-the-loop/software-in-the-loop (FMU/HIL) tied to requirements.
  * Variant/config management built-in (no ad hoc forks).
  * Event-driven change workflows with impact analysis (graph-based).
* **Acceptance criteria:**

  * Automatic **impact analysis** lists affected parts, tests, documents, work instructions within 30s for 99p cases.
  * **Trace completeness** ≥ 95% for “req ↔ design ↔ test” on released baselines.

## 2.2 Compliance demonstrable by construction

* **Objectives:**

  * **Evidence pack assembly time** (e.g., ISO 26262 safety case, DO-178C PSAC/SOI data) ↓ **60%**.
  * **Audit nonconformances** related to missing trace evidence ↓ **80%**.
* **Levers:**

  * Immutable baselines; signed approvals; automated V&V matrices from live links.
  * Standard templates for FMEA/FTA, hazard logs, and safety requirements.
* **Acceptance criteria:**

  * One-click **V&V matrix** generation that is fully reproducible from current graph state.
  * All signatures are eIDAS/ESIGN compliant; every approval has a machine-verifiable provenance trail.

## 2.3 Scalable collaboration with strong IP boundaries

* **Objectives:**

  * Onboard a tier-1 supplier to a shared program space in **<48 hours** with scoped visibility.
  * Zero “data leakage” incidents across suppliers (measured via policy violations).
* **Levers:**

  * Attribute-Based Access Control (ABAC) with policies on **project, artifact type, variant, classification**, and **export control** tags.
  * Contract-bound exchanges (API + event contracts) and supplier sandboxes.
* **Acceptance criteria:**

  * **Least-privilege defaults**; “what a supplier sees” is provably enumerated by policy simulation.
  * **Redaction/obfuscation** patterns (e.g., share geometry as JT/lightweight with selective masking).

## 2.4 Leverage Digital Twins at product, process, and system levels

* **Objectives:**

  * 100% of released products have registered **product twins** with configuration lineage to EBOM/SW.
  * **Process twin** coverage for top 3 critical manufacturing lines; **system twin** coverage for one complex multi-subsystem product line.
* **Levers:**

  * Twin registry aligned to the Digital Thread; FMU/FMI and analytics hooks; bidirectional change (design ↔ ops).
* **Acceptance criteria:**

  * For any field asset, the platform can show its **as-maintained configuration**, associated issues, telemetry KPIs, and open changes—within 5 seconds P95.
  * **Virtual commissioning** runs (executable models) linked to acceptance test procedures.

---

# 3) Value Pillars → Operating Principles, Capabilities, and KPIs

## 3.1 End-to-end traceability

* **Principles:** “Link first,” “No orphan artifacts,” “Typed links with intent.”
* **Capabilities:**

  * Global IDs, versioning, typed relations, baseline hashing, graph queries, coverage views (what’s untraced?).
  * Impact analysis (forward/backward), change packages with auto-suggested affected items.
* **KPIs:** Trace completeness %, mean impact analysis latency, % of changes shipped with full trace coverage, audit pass rate.

## 3.2 Model-Based Systems Engineering (MBSE)

* **Principles:** Models are source of truth; requirements are testable and executable; simulations are evidence.
* **Capabilities:**

  * SysML v2 authoring/import; ReqIF interchange; parametric constraints; interface contracts; variant modeling.
  * FMU orchestration with captured environments (containerized toolchains).
* **KPIs:** % requirements with linked models/tests, sim reproducibility rate, time from requirement change to updated sim evidence.

## 3.3 Secure collaboration

* **Principles:** Default deny; policy as code; verifiable sharing; minimal-copy data access.
* **Capabilities:**

  * SSO (OIDC), SCIM; ABAC (OPA policies); confidential computing options; export-control classification; supplier workspaces.
  * Share links with scoped, expiring capabilities; watermarking, view-only renderers for sensitive CAD.
* **KPIs:** Time to onboard partner, policy violation rate, external user activity SLOs, data egress audit completeness.

## 3.4 Real-time operations insight

* **Principles:** Close the loop; operational signals drive engineering priorities; latency budgets matter.
* **Capabilities:**

  * IIoT ingestion (OPC UA, MQTT Sparkplug), historian connectors; anomaly detection; linkage from alarms/NCs to design items and CAPA workflows.
* **KPIs:** Detection-to-corrective-action lead time, % ops events linked to design root cause, MTTR reduction attributed to insights.

## 3.5 Governed data fabric

* **Principles:** Contracts over chaos; metadata-first; everything queryable.
* **Capabilities:**

  * Canonical information model; schema registry; data lineage; glossary + ontology; PII/export-control tagging; retention and legal hold.
* **KPIs:** Schema compatibility incident rate, metadata coverage %, time to locate authoritative artifact, data quality scorecards.

## 3.6 Extensibility

* **Principles:** Stable interfaces; backward-compatibility windows; sandboxed plugins.
* **Capabilities:**

  * Public APIs (REST/gRPC/GraphQL), AsyncAPI events; micro-frontend SDK; app marketplace; webhooks; server plugins; model transformers (STEP, JT, ReqIF, FMI).
* **KPIs:** Partner apps count, SDK NPS, % upgrades without partner breakage, average time to integrate a new tool.

---

# 4) Scope

## 4.1 In-scope (initial 24 months, depth-first slices)

1. **Requirements ↔ ALM ↔ Test** with MBSE linkage and signed baselines.
2. **Change control (ECR/ECO)** with graph-based impact and release orchestration.
3. **PLM bridge** (parts/BOM, lightweight CAD view, change sync).
4. **Simulation orchestration** for FMUs; results provenance.
5. **Quality core** (FMEA, NC/CAPA) tied to design and process.
6. **Ops loop**: historian/IIoT ingestion, NC triggers, asset registry, basic digital twin.
7. **Compliance workbench** (V&V matrices, signatures, evidence packs).
8. **Extensibility**: SDK alpha → marketplace v1.

## 4.2 Out-of-scope (initially; plan for adapters)

* Native full-featured CAD/CAE authoring (use connectors and embedded viewers).
* Full ERP/MRP (integrate with SAP/Oracle; we own the engineering side + handoffs).
* Complete MES execution (we orchestrate and verify; OEM systems run the line).
* Generic enterprise office suite features (email, chat) beyond contextual comments.

## 4.3 Boundaries & Integration Assumptions

* **System of engagement** for engineering; **system of record** for specific domains may remain external (PLM/ERP). The Thread overlays them via IDs and contracts.
* Minimum viable bridges: GitHub/GitLab, Jira/Azure DevOps, Teamcenter/Windchill, SAP (cost centers/materials), historian (OSIsoft PI/Ignition), MQTT broker.

---

# 5) Users & Top Journeys (to validate vision)

* **Systems engineer:** Define needs → author SysML reqs → link to test cases → run FMU → approve baseline → generate safety evidence.
  *Success:* gaps panel = 0, evidence generated in <2 min.
* **Design engineer (Mech/EE/SW):** Receive change → see impact graph → update design → trigger CI/sim → handoff to PLM.
  *Success:* change turnaround < 3 days with full links.
* **Quality/Compliance:** Review FMEA, NC/CAPA → pull V&V pack for audit.
  *Success:* pack generation with zero manual stitching.
* **Manufacturing/Ops:** Alarm triggers NC → see linked design & recent change → start CAPA → feedback to requirements.
  *Success:* detection-to-CAPA open < 4 hours.
* **Supplier:** Access scoped artifacts → deliver design package → pass automated interface checks.
  *Success:* onboarded in < 48h; no access policy violations.

---

# 6) Success Metrics (roll-up)

* **Traceability coverage** ≥ 95% on released baselines.
* **Avg. change lead time** ↓ 35%; **rework defects** ↓ 30%.
* **Evidence pack assembly time** ↓ 60%; **audit findings** ↓ 80%.
* **Supplier onboarding time** < 48h; **policy violation rate** → 0.
* **Twin coverage**: 100% product, targeted process/system twins for critical lines.
* **User experience**: P95 core page latency < 1.0s; search < 2.0s; impact analysis < 30s.

---

# 7) Risks & How Vision Handles Them

* **Tool sprawl/lock-in:** Open standards (ReqIF, SysML v2, STEP, JT, OPC UA, MQTT Sparkplug, FMI). Adapters instead of monolith rewrites.
* **Compliance gaps:** Evidence-by-construction, signed baselines, immutable audit.
* **Security/IP leakage:** ABAC + policy simulation, redaction, watermarked renderers, export-control tagging.
* **Cultural adoption:** Opinionated golden paths, “gaps” dashboards, and automated wins (impact analysis, evidence packs) to incentivize use.

---

# 8) Glossary (vision-critical terms)

* **Digital Thread:** The governed, linked set of lifecycle artifacts and events enabling end-to-end traceability and reasoning.
* **Baseline:** Signed, immutable snapshot of a configuration across one or more domains.
* **Typed Link:** A relation with semantics (e.g., *verifies*, *satisfies*, *implements*).
* **Digital Twin:** Living digital representation of a product/process/system with configuration lineage and data bindings.
* **Evidence Pack:** Auto-generated compilation of artifacts proving compliance against a standard or contract.

---

Awesome—let’s turn “Stakeholders & Governance” into a concrete, working system you can stand up on day one and scale to hundreds of teams.

# 1) Primary Personas (goals, decisions, and success signals)

**Systems Engineers (SE / MBSE)**

* *Owns:* needs, requirements, interfaces, SysML v2 models, trade studies, variants.
* *Decisions:* requirement acceptance, interface contracts, allocation to subsystems.
* *Needs:* typed trace links, impact analysis, V&V matrices, model execution.
* *Success:* ≥95% trace coverage; change impact ≤30s; zero orphan requirements.

**Product Engineers**

* *Mechanical:* CAD/BOM conformity, DFM/DFA, tolerance stack-ups.
* *Electrical:* schematics/PCB/BOM, component derating, compliance (EMC).
* *Embedded:* HW/SW co-design, HAL, timing budgets, safety mechanisms.
* *Software:* backlog, CI/CD, quality gates, SBOM.
* *Success (all):* ECO lead time ↓35%; defect escape ↓30%; released baseline is reproducible.

**Project/Program Managers**

* *Owns:* scope, schedule, risk, cost, dependencies, capacity planning.
* *Decisions:* release go/no-go; replan triggers; supplier milestones.
* *Success:* schedule variance <5%; EV within ±10%; dependency slippage <2 PIs/year.

**Safety & Compliance**

* *Owns:* standards mapping (ISO 26262, DO-178C, IEC 61508, ISO 9001, etc.), safety cases, audits.
* *Decisions:* safety requirements acceptance, evidence pack approval.
* *Success:* audit findings ↓80%; evidence pack assembly time ↓60%.

**Test/Verification Engineers**

* *Owns:* test plans/cases/procedures, benches/Rigs/HIL, coverage, results provenance.
* *Decisions:* test acceptance, defect severity, verification signoff.
* *Success:* automated V&V matrix; reproducible results; coverage gaps = 0 at release.

**Manufacturing & OT**

* *Owns:* MBOM, routings, work instructions, SPC/quality data, alarms/NCs.
* *Decisions:* change readiness, process qualifications, line impacts.
* *Success:* detection→CAPA < 4h; scrap/rework trends improving; NCs linked to root cause.

**Suppliers (Tier 1–N)**

* *Owns:* contracted deliverables, interface conformance, design packages.
* *Decisions:* change requests on their scope, data releases to OEM.
* *Success:* onboard in <48h; zero policy violations; on-time/quality deliveries.

**Program Leadership (GM, Chief Engineer)**

* *Owns:* product vision, economics, portfolio bets, risk appetite.
* *Decisions:* trade-offs across cost/schedule/scope; escalation arbitration.
* *Success:* portfolio ROI; on-time launch; risk profile trending down.

**IT / InfoSec**

* *Owns:* identity, access, SaaS/on-prem posture, policy-as-code, audit trails.
* *Decisions:* exception handling, vendor approvals, key management.
* *Success:* zero critical vulns in prod; mean policy change lead time <24h.

---

# 2) Decision Rights & RACI (sample)

| Decision / Artifact                    | A (Accountable)         | R (Responsible)   | C (Consulted)          | I (Informed)    |
| -------------------------------------- | ----------------------- | ----------------- | ---------------------- | --------------- |
| Canonical data model & typed links     | Chief Architect         | Domain Architects | SE, Quality, Data Gov  | All squads      |
| Security policies (ABAC, data classes) | CISO / InfoSec Lead     | Security Eng      | Legal, Chief Architect | All             |
| Release go/no-go                       | GM / Chief Engineer     | PMO, QA Lead      | Domain Leads, Support  | Partners        |
| Supplier onboarding scope & access     | Program Leadership      | Supplier Mgr, IT  | Legal, Security        | Teams           |
| Compliance evidence templates          | Standards Council Chair | Compliance Eng    | SE, Test, QA           | All             |
| Marketplace app certification          | Ecosystem Forum Chair   | Partner Eng       | Security, Product      | Community       |
| Architectural exceptions               | Architecture Board      | Domain Team       | Security, Perf Eng     | Product Council |

> Tip: codify this RACI as a living page and embed links to the ADRs/RFCs that instantiate each decision.

---

# 3) Program Governance (mandates, cadences, artifacts)

## Architecture Board

* **Membership:** Chief Architect (chair), domain architects (Req/MBSE, ALM, PLM bridge, Twin, Quality), principal SRE, Security architect.
* **Mandate:** Guardrails, reference architecture, non-functional budgets, data contracts, exception process.
* **Cadence:** Weekly triage (60m), monthly deep dive (2h), quarterly architecture review (QAR).
* **Inputs:** RFCs, ADRs, perf/security findings, partner integration proposals.
* **Outputs:** Versioned guardrails, approved RFCs, reference impls, exception memos, architecture scorecard.
* **Decision rule:** Lazy consensus; if contested, simple majority; for breaking changes, supermajority (⅔).
* **Escalation:** To Product Council for customer impact; to Program Leadership for scope/cost trade-offs.

## Product Council

* **Membership:** GM (chair), Head of Product, PMs per product area, UX lead, Support/Success lead, Ops rep.
* **Mandate:** Prioritize outcomes, capacity allocation, roadmap, deprecation policy, tiering SLAs.
* **Cadence:** Bi-weekly portfolio review (90m); quarterly PI Objectives ratification.
* **Outputs:** Ordered backlog of Epics with WSJF scores, capacity split (new features vs tech debt vs compliance), public roadmap.

## Standards & Compliance Council

* **Membership:** Compliance lead (chair), Safety lead, QA, Legal/Privacy, SE lead, Test lead.
* **Mandate:** Map standards to controls, approve evidence templates, own audit readiness, QMS alignment.
* **Cadence:** Bi-weekly (60m); pre-release compliance gate per train.
* **Outputs:** Standard operating procedures (SOPs), evidence pack templates, signoff checklists, audit findings backlog.

## Open Ecosystem Forum

* **Membership:** Ecosystem PM (chair), Partner Eng, DevRel, select ISVs, strategic customers, community reps.
* **Mandate:** SDK roadmap, extension points, certification, sample apps, migration guides.
* **Cadence:** Monthly (90m) + quarterly partner summit.
* **Outputs:** SDK releases, certification criteria, partner portal content, “Breaking Changes” advisories.

> Governance anti-patterns to avoid: councils doubling as delivery teams; hidden decision-making; no decision logs; over-indexing on synchronous meetings.

---

# 4) Operating Model (product-line + SAFe/Lean portfolio)

## Team Topologies

* **Stream-aligned (Domain) Squads:** Own a vertical value stream (e.g., Requirements/MBSE, Change Control, Test/V&V, Digital Twin). 6–9 people each (PM, TL, 3–5 devs, QA, designer).
* **Platform Squads:** Identity/Access, Events/Kafka, Workflow/Temporal, Observability, Data Platform/Lakehouse, Graph/Traceability, SDK/DevPortal.
* **Integration Squads:** PLM bridges, ERP, MES/SCADA, CAD/CAE connectors, Historian/IIoT.
* **Enabling Squads:** Performance & Reliability, Security Enablement, Compliance Enablement.

## Agile Release Trains (ARTs)

* **ART-1 (Engineering Lifecycle):** Requirements↔ALM↔Test, Change Control, Compliance.
* **ART-2 (Data & Twin):** Graph/trace, Lakehouse, Analytics, Digital Twin, IIoT ingest.
* **ART-3 (Ecosystem & Integrations):** SDK, Marketplace, PLM/ERP/MES bridges.

**PI (Program Increment):** 10–12 weeks, 5 two-week iterations + 1 IP/innovation week.
**Ceremonies:** PI Planning (2 days), System Demo (end of each iteration), Inspect & Adapt (end of PI).

## Lean Portfolio Mgmt

* **Epic Kanban:** Funnel → Review → Analysis (lean business case) → Portfolio Backlog → Implementing → Done.
* **Prioritization:** WSJF (user/business value, time criticality, risk reduction/opportunity enablement, job size).
* **Capacity Allocation (per PI):** 60% features, 20% tech debt/quality, 10% compliance, 10% innovation (tune per quarter).
* **Guardrails:** Investment horizons, exit criteria per epic, minimum security/compliance budget floor.

---

# 5) Lifecycle Controls & Stage Gates (evidence-by-construction)

**Gate 0 – Charter**

* *Artifacts:* Problem statement, measurable outcomes, KPIs, RACI, risks, initial ADR-000 (architecture decision to proceed).
* *Approvals:* Product Council (scope), Architecture Board (feasibility).

**Gate 1 – Architecture Readiness**

* *Artifacts:* C4 diagrams, data contracts (AsyncAPI/OpenAPI), NFR budgets, threat model (STRIDE), test strategy.
* *Approvals:* Architecture Board; Security sign-off for initial policies.

**Gate 2 – Compliance Plan**

* *Artifacts:* Standard mapping (e.g., ISO 26262 Part 6 controls), evidence templates, V&V matrix plan.
* *Approvals:* Standards & Compliance Council.

**Gate 3 – Release Readiness**

* *Artifacts:* Signed baseline, V&V matrix, performance report, SBOM + provenance (SLSA), DR/BC test results.
* *Approvals:* Product Council (business), Compliance (standards), Security (vulns ≤ defined threshold).

**Gate 4 – Operate**

* *Artifacts:* SLOs & error budgets, runbooks, on-call rota, post-release review plan.
* *Approvals:* SRE lead; Product for launch comms.

---

# 6) Supplier & Partner Governance

* **Onboarding:** DPA/processing agreements, security questionnaire, SOC2/ISO attestation, export-control tags, sandbox tenant creation, policy simulation (what they can see), audit log hooks.
* **Data Exchange:** Contracted APIs/events, schema versions, conformance tests, redaction (e.g., JT lightweight for CAD), IP watermarking.
* **Performance & Quality:** SLAs/OLAs, delivery acceptance criteria, interface tests in CI, supplier scorecard (on-time, defects, policy violations).
* **Certification (Marketplace):** Static analysis, dependency policy, security review, performance test, UX criteria, privacy review, versioned contract tests.

---

# 7) Security & Risk Governance (with InfoSec embedded)

* **Policy-as-Code:** OPA/Gatekeeper for ABAC and cluster policy; pre-merge checks.
* **Secure SDLC:** Threat modeling at Gate 1, SAST/DAST, dependency scanning, SBOM (CycloneDX), provenance (Sigstore/SLSA L3+ target).
* **Access & Secrets:** OIDC/SCIM, JIT access, per-tenant KMS keys, HSM-backed signing for baselines.
* **Reviews:** Security exception board (weekly); red-team exercises (semi-annual); incident simulations (quarterly).

---

# 8) Communication, Documentation, and Change Control

* **Decision Records:** ADRs (architecture), CDRs (compliance decision records), stored in a public repo per program with immutable IDs.
* **RFC Process:** Lightweight template → async review (72h) → Architecture Board decision → changelog entry.
* **Status Radiators:** Live OKR dashboards; PI objectives burn-up; governance scorecards; “Breaking Changes” bulletin.
* **Escalation Ladder:** Squad → Domain lead → Architecture/Product councils → Program Leadership; documented SLAs for responses (e.g., 48h for blocking escalations).

---

# 9) Metrics & Health Checks (governance as a product)

* **Flow:** Lead time for change, deployment frequency, change fail rate, MTTR (by stream).
* **Governance:** % decisions with ADRs, average RFC cycle time, % exceptions closed within PI, audit readiness index.
* **Security/Compliance:** Open critical vulns, SBOM freshness, policy violation rate, evidence pack freshness (days since out-of-date).
* **Collaboration:** Supplier onboarding time, partner certification throughput, NPS (internal & partner).
* **Performance/NFRs:** P95 latency for core pages, impact analysis SLA, availability per ART.

---

# 10) Staffing & Org Seed (first 2 PIs, indicative)

* **Leadership:** GM, Chief Architect, Head of Product, Compliance Lead, Security Lead, Head of SRE, Partner/Ecosystem Lead.
* **Squads (initial):**

  * 4 Stream-aligned: Req/MBSE; Change & Release; Test/V&V; Digital Twin.
  * 4 Platform: Identity/Access; Events & Workflow; Graph/Trace; Data Platform.
  * 3 Integration: PLM Bridge; ERP/MES; IIoT/SCADA.
* **Size:** ~11 squads × 7 people ≈ 77 ICs + leadership/PM/UX/SRE (~25) ≈ **~100–110 FTE** to start.

---

# 11) Templates & Checklists (ready-to-use)

**ADR Template (one-pager)**

* Context, Decision, Options considered, Consequences, Owners, Review date, Link to RFC/tests.

**RFC Template**

* Problem, Proposed change, Affected services/contracts, Backwards compatibility, Security/Privacy impact, Rollout plan, Revert plan.

**Gate 3 (Release) Checklist (excerpt)**

* ✅ Baseline signed (hash + approvers)
* ✅ V&V matrix coverage ≥ target
* ✅ Perf report meets NFR budgets
* ✅ SBOM published & provenance signed
* ✅ Runbooks updated; on-call trained
* ✅ “Breaking Changes” notice published

---

# 12) How it all fits together (day-in-the-life)

1. SE raises an RFC to add a new link type (*mitigates hazard*).
2. Architecture Board approves; Standards Council maps it into evidence templates.
3. Platform Graph team ships contract tests; Domain squads adopt with a PI objective.
4. Product Council allocates capacity; Integration squads update exporters.
5. Partners get notified via Ecosystem Forum; certification tests updated.
6. At release, Compliance pulls a pack with the new link type—zero manual stitching.

Amazing—here’s a practical, soup-to-nuts expansion of the **Core Capabilities**. For each module you’ll get: purpose, key objects, core workflows, integrations & events, data contracts/APIs, UI highlights, governance & security notes, KPIs/SLOs, and acceptance tests. Everything is designed to snap into the Digital Thread.

---

# 1) Requirements & MBSE

**Purpose**
Author, manage, and trace needs → requirements → architecture → interfaces → verification, with SysML v2 at the core and ReqIF for exchange.

**Key objects**
`Need`, `Requirement`, `Constraint`, `UseCase`, `Function`, `Block`, `Interface`, `Variant`, `TradeStudy`, `Risk`, `Baseline`.

**Core workflows**

* Author requirements (rich text + structure), allocate to architecture blocks, define interfaces & constraints.
* Variants/config: feature models, rules (“if market=EU then add EMC reqs”).
* Trade studies with scored alternatives and decision rationale linked to requirements.
* Baseline + sign: eID-compliant signatures, cryptographic hash.
* Coverage & gaps panel: shows items without upstream/downstream links.

**Integrations & events**

* **To ALM:** auto-create epics/stories/tests from requirements; keep status in sync.
* **To PLM:** release handoff; change requests round-trip.
* **To Sim/Verification:** simulation scenarios generated from requirement parameters.
* **Events:** `RequirementCreated`, `RequirementChanged`, `RequirementBaselined`, `InterfaceChanged`, `VariantRuleUpdated`.

**APIs & data contracts**

* REST/GraphQL for CRUD; AsyncAPI for events.
* Typed links (`satisfies`, `verifies`, `implements`, `derivedFrom`, `mitigates`) carry: `sourceId`, `targetId`, `type`, `confidence`, `createdBy`, `createdAt`.
* ReqIF import/export with mapping to internal schema; SysML v2 import of packages and diagrams (stored as models + renders).

**UI highlights**

* Dual-pane **Model + Trace** view; drag-drop linking; variant toggles.
* **Impact explorer**: graph lens to view ripple effects from a change.
* **Evidence builder**: live V&V matrix filtered by baseline.

**Governance & security**

* ABAC policies by project, classification (e.g., export-controlled), variant.
* Required fields & review gates per requirement class (safety, regulatory).

**KPIs/SLOs**

* Traceability coverage ≥ 95% on release baselines.
* Impact analysis P95 < 30s for 10k artifacts.
* Req import (ReqIF) fidelity ≥ 99% fields mapped.

**Acceptance tests**

* Given a changed requirement, platform lists affected tests, simulations, parts, work instructions within 30s and opens a change package with them pre-populated.

---

# 2) ALM / Software Engineering

**Purpose**
Plan and execute software work with safety-ready traceability and CI/CD hooks.

**Key objects**
`Epic`, `Story`, `Task`, `Bug`, `TestCase`, `TestRun`, `Build`, `Release`, `SBOM`, `SafetyRequirement`.

**Core workflows**

* Backlog management with WSJF; link stories ↔ requirements; autogenerate test stubs.
* CI/CD integration (GitHub/GitLab/Azure DevOps) captures builds, test results, coverage, static analysis, artifacts, SBOM.
* Safety pathways: enforce coding standards, coverage targets, two-person reviews, evidence packs for ISO 26262/DO-178C.

**Integrations & events**

* **From MBSE:** create epics/tests; update verification status.
* **To QA/Compliance:** push evidence artifacts.
* **Events:** `BuildCompleted`, `TestRunCompleted`, `ReleaseCreated`, `SBOMPublished`.

**APIs**

* Webhooks for CI events; REST to post test results (xUnit/JUnit), coverage (Cobertura/JaCoCo), SBOM (CycloneDX).
* Policy API: per-repo gates (coverage ≥ X, vuln severity ≤ Y, reviewers ≥ Z).

**UI highlights**

* **Trace-aware backlog** badges: shows linked requirements/tests already covered/not covered.
* **Evidence view**: one screen to see test coverage, static analysis, SBOM issues for a release.

**Governance & security**

* Signed builds & provenance (SLSA-aligned); artifact retention policies.
* Differential approvals for safety-critical code areas.

**KPIs/SLOs**

* Change fail rate, deployment frequency, MTTR; coverage targets by safety level (ASIL/B/C/D, DAL A-E).
* P95 “commit→test results visible” < 5 min.

**Acceptance tests**

* A DO-178C release shows objective evidence (trace to HLR/LLR, structural coverage) and passes automated gate checks before “Release” can be marked done.

---

# 3) PLM / CAD / CAE Connect

**Purpose**
Bridge engineering data to PLM/PDM, manage parts and BOMs, control changes, and orchestrate CAE runs.

**Key objects**
`Part`, `EBOM`, `MBOM`, `Document`, `ChangeRequest (ECR)`, `ChangeOrder (ECO)`, `CADFile`, `CAEJob`, `Material`, `SupplierPart`.

**Core workflows**

* Part creation & classification; EBOM authoring; effectivity/variants; MBOM alignment.
* Change control: ECR triage → ECO execution with impacted items auto-listed.
* CAD/PDM integration: view JT/lightweight renders, redaction; watermarking.
* CAE orchestration: run simulations on clusters; store inputs/outputs & provenance.

**Integrations & events**

* PLM bridges (Teamcenter/Windchill/3DEXPERIENCE): sync parts/BOMs/changes.
* CAD gateways (NX, CATIA, SolidWorks) for metadata + viewer.
* **Events:** `PartReleased`, `BOMUpdated`, `ECOApproved`, `CAEJobCompleted`.

**APIs**

* PLM connectors via vendor APIs; file vault via object storage with dedupe; CAE job API (submit, monitor, retrieve artifacts), supports FMU interfaces.

**UI highlights**

* **BOM compare** with diff on structure, attributes, cost deltas.
* **Change package** view with automatic impact suggestions.

**Governance & security**

* Export-control tagging; view-only renders for external users; watermarking.
* ECO requires approvals from affected domains; e-signatures logged.

**KPIs/SLOs**

* ECR→ECO lead time; % ECOs with full trace links; CAE job success rate; P95 BOM open < 1.5s for 50k items.

**Acceptance tests**

* On ECO approval, EBOM/MBOM deltas, updated work instructions, and affected tests are linked and versioned automatically.

---

# 4) Simulation & Verification

**Purpose**
Run, manage, and prove simulations and tests as evidence.

**Key objects**
`Scenario`, `ParameterSet`, `Model`, `FMU`, `SimulationRun`, `TestCase`, `TestResult`, `CoverageReport`, `Rig/HIL`, `ArtifactProvenance`.

**Core workflows**

* Scenario library by domain (functional safety, performance, environmental).
* Orchestrate FMU/Simulink/Modelica/CFD/FEA runs; cache results; compare baselines.
* Verification management: map requirements → test cases → results → coverage.

**Integrations & events**

* Pulls requirement parameters; pushes verification status to MBSE/ALM.
* HIL bench integration for physical test results ingestion.
* **Events:** `SimulationRunCompleted`, `VerificationStatusChanged`.

**APIs**

* Run submission (container image + inputs), deterministic seeds; results stored with digests.
* Results schema includes `inputs`, `toolchain`, `hashes`, `logs`, `metrics`.

**UI highlights**

* **Scenario grid** that shows pass/fail trends per baseline.
* **Provenance inspector**: all inputs, seeds, tool versions.

**Governance & security**

* Reproducibility checks; toolchain signing; compute quotas; access to sensitive models controlled by policy.

**KPIs/SLOs**

* Reproducibility rate ≥ 99%; P95 run metadata retrieval < 2s; coverage against verification plan ≥ 95%.

**Acceptance tests**

* Clicking a requirement opens its scenario list and latest passing result with evidence artifacts; regenerating the run with same params yields identical metrics.

---

# 5) Quality, Risk & Compliance

**Purpose**
Manage risks (FMEA/FTA), nonconformances, corrective actions, audits, and produce compliance evidence by construction.

**Key objects**
`Hazard`, `Risk`, `FMEAItem`, `FTAEvent`, `Control`, `NCR`, `CAPA`, `Audit`, `InspectionPlan`, `EvidencePack`.

**Core workflows**

* FMEA: failure modes → effects → controls → actions; auto-link to design items and tests.
* NCR/CAPA: detect → contain → correct → verify → prevent; linked to ops data and design changes.
* Audit prep: assemble evidence from live links; sign and lock packs.

**Integrations & events**

* From ops (SPC, alarms) create NCRs; to MBSE/ALM/PLM for corrective actions.
* **Events:** `NCRCreated`, `CAPAClosed`, `RiskLevelChanged`, `EvidencePackGenerated`.

**APIs**

* Risk scoring calculator (configurable RPN/ASIL/DAL semantics).
* Evidence pack generator API (inputs: baseline, standard; output: PDF/JSON bundle).

**UI highlights**

* **Risk heatmap** with drill-downs to linked design/tests.
* **CAPA board** with SLA timers and effectivity checks.

**Governance & security**

* Immutable audit trails; role-restricted risk edits; calibration of scoring models governed by Standards Council.

**KPIs/SLOs**

* Audit findings/NCs trend; CAPA lead time; risk reduction velocity; evidence pack build time P95 < 2 min.

**Acceptance tests**

* Given an NCR from line 3, system proposes linked design change and affected tests; closing CAPA verifies test passes and updates FMEA controls.

---

# 6) Manufacturing & Operations

**Purpose**
Bridge engineering to the shop floor and the field; ensure design intent executes and feedback closes the loop.

**Key objects**
`WorkInstruction`, `Routing`, `Operation`, `Resource`, `SPCChart`, `Alarm`, `ShiftReport`, `AssetEvent`, `MaterialLot`.

**Core workflows**

* Publish work instructions tied to MBOM revision and effectivity dates.
* Ingest MES/MOM execution data and historian signals; detect anomalies; trigger NCR/CAPA.
* Digital signoff at station; e-traveler with embedded inspections.

**Integrations & events**

* MES/MOM connectors (Opcenter, Ignition, etc.); historians (PI/Ignition/Timeseries DB).
* IIoT via OPC UA & MQTT Sparkplug B; edge agents with buffering.
* **Events:** `WorkInstructionPublished`, `AlarmRaised`, `ProcessCapabilityChanged`.

**APIs**

* Ingestion endpoints for time-series and events; schema mapping with unit normalization.
* Work instruction API (resolve by serial/lot → correct revision).

**UI highlights**

* **Line view**: WIP, OEE, alarms; click through to linked design changes.
* **Instruction viewer** with revision & effectivity badges.

**Governance & security**

* Edge trust (device identity, certs); offline operation; data residency controls.
* Read-only views for suppliers; station operators see only necessary instructions.

**KPIs/SLOs**

* Detection→CAPA open < 4h; instruction retrieval P95 < 1s; data lag from line < 60s.

**Acceptance tests**

* Changing torque spec in MBOM updates work instruction; next job at station sees new instruction with effectivity; SPC limits auto-update.

# 7) Digital Twin & Digital Thread

**Purpose**
Create living twins with lineage to design/production/service; maintain the Thread graph for reasoning and impact.

**Key objects**
`Twin (product/process/system)`, `TwinState`, `TelemetryBinding`, `MaintenanceRecord`, `ConfigurationSnapshot`, `ThreadLink`.

**Core workflows**

* Register twins on release; bind telemetry; maintain as-maintained configuration.
* Twin-of-twins composition for complex systems and lines.
* Virtual commissioning and what-if using executable models.

**Integrations & events**

* From PLM/MES for as-built; from ops for state; from MBSE for models.
* **Events:** `TwinRegistered`, `TwinConfigChanged`, `TelemetryBound`, `TwinAlert`.

**APIs**

* Twin registry CRUD; query by serial, asset tag, or lineage; graph traversal queries (“show upstream requirements for this failing asset”).
* Telemetry mapping (tag → semantic signal → unit).

**UI highlights**

* **Twin overview**: config, KPIs, open CAPAs, linked changes.
* **Thread map**: clickable path from field issue → design artifacts.

**Governance & security**

* Data minimization for field PII; tenant isolation; time-boxed data retention per policy.

**KPIs/SLOs**

* % of shipped assets registered; config drift detection rate; mean diagnosis time using thread queries.

**Acceptance tests**

* For a serial number, show as-maintained config, last service, open NCRs, and upstream requirements within 5s.

## Cross-cutting link types (canonical)

`derivesFrom`, `satisfies`, `implements`, `verifies`, `refines`, `allocatedTo`, `affectsVariant`, `mitigates`, `causes`, `dependsOn`, `produces`, `consumes`, `asBuiltOf`, `asMaintainedOf`.

## Non-functional guardrails (applies to all)

* **Latency targets:** P95 < 1s for primary reads; < 2s for heavy views; background jobs async.
* **Scale:** Millions of artifacts per tenant; billions of events in lakehouse; 10k concurrent users.
* **Security:** OIDC/SCIM; ABAC via OPA; per-tenant keys; immutable audit trails; SBOM/provenance for every release.
* **Interoperability:** SysML v2, ReqIF, STEP/JT, FMI/FMU, OPC UA, MQTT Sparkplug B, AsyncAPI/OpenAPI.

---

## 4) Non-Functional Requirements

* **Security & Privacy**: Zero-trust, OIDC/OAuth2, SCIM, ABAC/RBAC, tenant isolation, data residency, supply-chain security (SLSA), SBOM.
* **Compliance**: SOC2, ISO 27001, ISO 9001, GxP, industry-specific (e.g., IEC 61508, ISO 26262, DO-178C/DO-254 support).
* **Performance & Scale**: 10k+ concurrent users/tenant; sub-second UI for common flows; petabyte-scale data lakehouse; billions of events/day.
* **Reliability**: Multi-region HA; RPO ≤ 5 min, RTO ≤ 30 min.
* **Extensibility**: Stable versioned APIs, event contracts, plugin sandboxing.
* **Interoperability**: Open standards first (SysML, ReqIF, STEP, JT, OPC UA, MQTT Sparkplug, ISO 15926, FMI/FMU).
* **Auditability**: Immutable trails, cryptographic signing of baselines.

Awesome—here’s a concrete, “buildable” **Reference Architecture** for the platform. I’ve expanded every layer with responsibilities, interfaces, patterns, scale/SLA targets, and example flows so teams can start carving work immediately.

---

# 1) Experience Layer

**Scope**

* Web UI (React + Module Federation micro-frontends), native mobile (critical field ops), and thick-client connectors (CAD/IDE plug-ins).
* Command palette for power users; full **a11y** (WCAG 2.1 AA) and **i18n/l10n**.

**Key components**

* **Shell/Composition App**: hosts route registry, global nav, theming, auth session, feature flags, telemetry bootstrap.
* **Micro-frontends (MFEs)**: Requirements, Change, Test, BOM, Quality, Twin, Ops, Analytics, Portfolio, Compliance.
* **BFFs (Backends for Frontends)** per slice:

  * GraphQL gateway for read-heavy “screen models”.
  * REST for mutating actions; websocket/SSE for live updates.
* **Connectors**:

  * **CAD** (NX/CATIA/SW) plug-ins for metadata capture, check-in/out, watermarking.
  * **IDE** (VS Code, JetBrains) extensions: requirements peek, trace link hints, policy gates in CI.
* **Command Palette**

  * Global actions (“Create Change Package”, “Generate Evidence Pack”).
  * Fuzzy entity search across artifact graph.

**Non-functional targets**

* P95 route change ≤ **1.0s** (warm), ≤ **1.5s** (cold).
* Largest Contentful Paint (desktop) ≤ **2.5s** on standard corp network.
* 100% accessibility checks in CI; locale packs lazy-loaded.

**Security**

* OIDC/OAuth2; short-lived access tokens + silent refresh; Content Security Policy locked down.
* Per-view **policy probes** to grey-out controls the user cannot exercise.

**Failure patterns**

* Offline cache for field UIs (read-only views, queued actions).
* Feature flag kill-switch per MFE.

---

# 2) Domain Apps

**Scope** (vertical slices)

* Requirements/MBSE, ALM, PLM Bridge, Simulation, Quality, Compliance, MES/SCADA Ops, Portfolio.

**Pattern**

* Each app owns:

  * **UI MFE + BFF**.
  * A set of **Domain Services** (below).
  * A small **projection store** (read models) optimized for its screens.
* **API style**

  * Read: GraphQL (federated) with entity ownership per domain.
  * Write: REST/gRPC commands; asynchronous replies via events.

**Cross-cutting**

* **Review & Approval** widget (reused).
* **Decision Log** and **Comment** widgets (embedded everywhere).
* **Context panel** that shows upstream/downstream links from the Thread graph.

---

# 3) Domain Services (DDD bounded contexts)

**Common contract**

* CRUD + behavior endpoints; events for state changes; outbox + idempotency.
* **Resource naming**: `/v1/{context}/{aggregate}/{id}`
* **Events** are canonical (see Events section).

**Key services & responsibilities**

* **Requirements**: requirement sets, interfaces, variants, baselines, ReqIF/SysML import.
* **Test**: test cases/runs/results, coverage, rigs/HIL integration.
* **Change**: ECR/ECO workflow, impact analysis orchestration.
* **Part/BOM**: parts, EBOMs/MBOMs, effectivity, cost roll-ups.
* **Configuration/Variants**: feature models, rules, variant resolution.
* **Simulation Runs**: scenario lib, job orchestration, provenance.
* **Nonconformance**: NCRs, containment → CAPA hooks.
* **FMEA/FTA**: risk registry, scoring models, action tracking.
* **Work Instructions**: authoring, effectivity, station routing.
* **Digital Twin**: registry, as-built/as-maintained snapshots, telemetry bindings.
* **Asset Registry**: equipment/lines, calibration, availability.

**Storage patterns**

* OLTP per service (Postgres by default).
* **Graph sidecar** updates via events for cross-domain traceability.
* Projections (read models) for UI: Elastic/OpenSearch indices per screen.

**Performance budgets**

* Command latency P95 ≤ **200 ms** (in-region).
* Hot read P95 ≤ **50 ms** from projection stores.

---

# 4) Platform Services

## 4.1 Workflow & Rules

* **Temporal** (micro-workflows, sagas) + **BPMN 2.0** for business flows.
* **DMN** rules for variant resolution, risk scoring, approval routing.
* **API**: `POST /v1/workflows/{type}/start`, signal/query endpoints; rules evaluate with versioned decision tables.

## 4.2 Events & Streaming

* **Kafka** backbone; **Schema Registry** (Avro/Protobuf) with compatibility policies.
* Topic taxonomy:

  * `dom.{context}.{aggregate}.evt` (e.g., `dom.requirements.req.evt`)
  * `dom.{context}.cmd` for async commands (rare; mostly REST/gRPC).
  * `int.{system}.cdc` for CDC streams (Debezium).
* **Semantics**

  * Producer transactions + idempotent consumers for exactly-once where needed.
  * Partition keys chosen for ordering guarantees (e.g., aggregate id).
* **DLQ** & replay

  * Per-topic DLQs; replay tooling with time or offset windows.

## 4.3 Search & Discovery

* OpenSearch clusters with:

  * **Index per view** pattern (denormalized docs).
  * Synonym sets per domain; analyzers per language.
  * Security: document-level filtering via precomputed ACL fields.

## 4.4 Identity & Access

* **AuthN**: OIDC; **Provisioning**: SCIM.
* **AuthZ**: ABAC with OPA (Rego policies). Resource attributes (project, classification, export control, variant, tenant).
* **Policy simulation** endpoint for “what would user X see?”

## 4.5 File/Model Storage

* Object storage (S3-compatible) with **content-addressable** keys, dedupe, and server-side encryption.
* **Virus scanning**, **DLP**, **watermarking** for external shares.
* Secure viewers: CAD (JT/glTF), PDF, images; large-file ranged reads.

## 4.6 Observability

* OpenTelemetry everywhere (traces, metrics, logs).
* **SLOs** declared per service; error budgets tracked; golden signals dashboards.
* Trace + log correlation (trace id propagated to log lines).

## 4.7 NLG/NLP

* Doc generation service:

  * Templating (Jinja/Handlebars) + graph queries → PDFs/HTML with signatures.
  * NLP utilities: entity extraction for legacy imports, trace gap detection, auto-summaries.

---

# 5) Data Layer

## 5.1 Operational DBs

* **Postgres** per service (schema-per-service), HA with Patroni; point-in-time recovery.
* **Temporal** DB (Postgres) for workflow state (separate cluster).
* **Graph DB** (Neo4j/JanusGraph) for the Digital Thread:

  * Write via event consumers; read for deep traversals and impact analysis.
  * **Sharding** by tenant; hot cache for common traversals.
* **Time-series** (Timescale/VictoriaMetrics) for historian and telemetry.

## 5.2 Lakehouse

* **Apache Iceberg** (or Delta) tables on object storage.
* Ingest via Kafka → Flink → Iceberg; schema evolution guarded by Registry.
* Compute: **Trino**/Spark for ad hoc + scheduled analytics.
* **Governance**: Apache Atlas/Amundsen catalogs; lineage from events and ETL jobs.

## 5.3 Knowledge Graph

* Option A: RDF/OWL with SHACL constraints; Option B: LPG with ontology layer.
* **Mappings**: ReqIF ↔ SysML v2, STEP/JT ↔ Part/BOM, FMI↔Sim.
* Serves semantic queries and doc generation templates.

**Data protection**

* Per-tenant KMS keys; field-level encryption for sensitive attrs; data residency placements.

**Backup/DR**

* RPO ≤ **5 min** (WAL shipping + object storage versioning), RTO ≤ **30 min** per region; cross-region disaster drills quarterly.

---

# 6) Edge & OT

**Pattern**

* **Edge agents** (containers) for:

  * OPC UA client, MQTT (Sparkplug B), local buffering (SQLite/RocksDB), compression.
  * Transform (units, quality flags), sign messages, backpressure handling.
* **Brokers**: HiveMQ/EMQX clusters with TLS mutual auth, per-tenant namespaces, retained LWT topics.
* **Offline mode**

  * Persistent queue; exactly-once to cloud via producer transactions.
* **Remote management**

  * Secure OTA updates, key rotation, device posture health.

**Security**

* X.509 per device; attestation on connect; policy to fence “chatty” devices.
* Network isolation (no inbound from edge to plant networks).

**Latency/scale**

* Ingest ≥ **200k msgs/s** per region; end-to-end (edge→analytics) P95 < **10s** for high-priority tags.

---

# 7) Infrastructure

**Kubernetes**

* Multi-cluster, multi-region; one **control plane** per region; namespaces per tenant + platform.
* **Service mesh** (Istio): mTLS, retries/timeouts, circuit breakers, traffic shifting for canaries.

**GitOps**

* ArgoCD for app deploys; promotions via PRs between env repos.
* **Policies as code**: OPA/Gatekeeper for cluster and workload policies (images, privileges, network).

**Secrets**

* Vault + CSI driver; envelope encryption; short-lived DB creds via Vault.

**Build & Supply Chain**

* SBOM (CycloneDX) on every build; signed images (Sigstore cosign); provenance (SLSA L3+ target).

**Cost & Capacity**

* Horizontal/vertical autoscaling; priority classes (prod > batch > sandbox).
* Cost dashboards by tenant and service.

---

# Event-Driven Integration Pattern (in depth)

**Why**

* Decouple services, enable real-time traceability, support replayable audit.

**Canonical events (examples)**

```json
// dom.requirements.req.evt
{
  "eventId": "uuid",
  "eventType": "RequirementChanged",
  "aggregateId": "req-123",
  "tenantId": "t-001",
  "version": 7,
  "occurredAt": "2025-11-04T12:00:00Z",
  "actor": {"id":"u-42","type":"user"},
  "data": {
    "title": "Brake response time",
    "severity": "Safety",
    "linksAdded": [{"type":"verifies","targetId":"test-889"}]
  },
  "schemaVersion": "1.2.0"
}
```

```json
// dom.plm.change.evt
{
  "eventType": "ChangeApproved",
  "aggregateId": "eco-55",
  "data": {"baseline":"base-2025-10-12","affectedParts":["p-1","p-2"]}
}
```

```json
// dom.twin.asset.evt
{
  "eventType": "TwinUpdated",
  "aggregateId": "sn-ABC123",
  "data": {"configDelta":{"param":"maxTorque","old":50,"new":55}}
}
```

**Standards**

* Versioned schemas; **backward-compatible** by default.
* **Outbox pattern** in every service; transactional publish on commit.
* **Idempotency**: `eventId` + dedupe table per consumer group.
* **Ordering**: key by aggregate for strict ordering; cross-aggregate sagas via Temporal.

**CDC**

* Debezium for bridging 3rd-party systems (PLM/ERP); transform to canonical events before distribution.

**Dead letters & replay**

* DLQ topics with reason; replay tool requires “compaction safety” (no destructive changes to consumers).

---

# Example end-to-end flows

## A) Requirement change → impact → approval

1. **Requirements Service** persists change, emits `RequirementChanged`.
2. **Graph Updater** consumes, mutates Thread edges; **Search** updates projections.
3. **Change Service** listens, prebuilds an **Impact Set** (tests, parts, work instructions) and proposes a change package.
4. **Workflow** launches an approval BPMN; **Rules** decide approvers (safety → compliance needed).
5. On approval, **NLG** generates updated V&V matrix; **Events**: `ChangeApproved`, `BaselineCreated`.

**SLO**: impact set available in **≤ 30s** P95.

## B) Shop-floor torque alarm → CAPA

1. **Edge** publishes Sparkplug message → **Ingest** → **Time-series DB**.
2. **Rules** raise NCR; **Nonconformance Service** emits `NCRCreated`.
3. **Graph** links NCR ↔ part ↔ recent ECO; **Quality App** proposes CAPA tasks.
4. **Work Instructions** are updated (new torque spec), versioned, and pushed to stations.

**SLO**: detection → CAPA open **< 4h** (operational), instruction change visible **< 15 min**.

## C) Supplier app install

1. **Marketplace** verifies app, permission manifest, signs artifact.
2. **Extension Runtime** creates sandbox, issues scoped tokens.
3. **MFE** of app becomes available; server plugin subscribes to **read-only** events.

**Guardrail**: app cannot exfiltrate raw CAD; access via viewer streams only.

---

# Tenancy, data residency, and boundaries

* **Multi-tenant SaaS** default, **dedicated single-tenant** and **air-gapped** options.
* Hard isolation: namespace + DB schema + KMS keys per tenant; soft limits via quotas.
* **Residency**: data placed per tenant’s region; cross-region analytics are opt-in with anonymization.

---

# Performance guardrails (global)

* Read P95 (hot views) ≤ **1s**; search ≤ **2s**.
* Impact analysis graph traversal (≤ 5 hops, 10k nodes) ≤ **30s** P95.
* Evidence pack generation ≤ **2 min** P95.
* Kafka end-to-end (producer→consumer) median **< 500 ms** intra-region.

---

# Security by design (highlights)

* mTLS everywhere (mesh), JWT → SPIFFE/SPIRE optional for workload IDs.
* Resource tagging: classification/export-control; policies enforced at API and search layers.
* **Provenance**: every baseline signed; image/build provenance recorded (SLSA).
* **Secrets** rotated automatically; JIT admin via break-glass with audit.

---

# Build/run toolchain (opinionated)

* **Backend**: Java 21, Spring Boot 3, gRPC/REST, Temporal, Kafka.
* **Frontend**: TypeScript/React, Module Federation, GraphQL (Apollo Federation).
* **Data**: Postgres, Neo4j, Iceberg + Trino, OpenSearch, Timescale.
* **Infra**: K8s, Istio, ArgoCD, Vault, OPA, OpenTelemetry.

---

# “Ready to implement” acceptance checks

* ☑️ A new domain service boots with:

  * health, metrics, trace, pprof; OpenAPI + AsyncAPI; outbox enabled; policy stub.
* ☑️ An event schema PR must include:

  * compat report, example payloads, data classification, consumer impact notes.
* ☑️ Any new MFE:

  * a11y checks, i18n hooks, telemetry wired, feature flag, BFF contract tests.
* ☑️ A new baseline:

  * hash + signatures, reproducible build record, evidence pack regenerable from live graph.

Awesome—here’s a build-ready **Data & Digital Twin Strategy** you can hand to platform/data/domain teams. I’ve detailed the canonical model, graph semantics, contracts/governance, twin patterns, and historian pipeline—plus KPIs and acceptance tests so you know it works.

# 1) Canonical Information Model (CIM)

**Purpose:** one language across Requirements → Design → Verification → Manufacturing/Ops → Service. Implemented as:

* **Operational schemas** (Postgres per service),
* **Canonical events** (Avro/Protobuf),
* **Knowledge/Ontology layer** (RDF/OWL or LPG ontology) for cross-domain semantics.

## 1.1 Global rules

* **Global IDs:** `urn:omni:{tenant}:{type}:{namespace}:{ulid}` (ULID for time-sortable uniqueness).
* **Versioning:** semantic (`MAJOR.MINOR.PATCH`) per aggregate; immutable commits, mutable heads via new versions.
* **Timestamps:** RFC 3339 UTC; monotonic clocks at write; clock-skew compensators for merges.
* **Classification:** `{classification:[internal|confidential|export_controlled], domain, safety_level}` embedded in records & events.
* **Signatures:** baselines and evidence packs are signed (detached, COSE/DSSE) with tenant KMS keys.

## 1.2 Core entities (minimal fields—extend per domain)

**Requirement**

* `id`, `title`, `text`, `type` (need|safety|performance…), `priority`, `state`, `variantExpr`, `links[]`, `owner`, `baselineIds[]`, `standards[]`
* Exchange: ReqIF map; SysML v2 package refs.

**DesignItem**

* Any artifact under design control: `id`, `type` (block|interface|schema|drawing), `specRef`, `owner`, `variants`, `maturity`.

**Part**

* `partNo`, `rev`, `class`, `make/buy`, `uom`, `approvedSuppliers[]`, `attributes{mass, cost, material}`, `effectivity`.

**BOM (EBOM/MBOM)**

* `id`, `type` (EBOM|MBOM), `lines[]:{parent, child, qty, uom, altGroup, effectivity}`.

**Variant/FeatureModel**

* `features[]`, `constraints` (SAT-exprs), `rules` (DMN table refs).

**Change (ECR/ECO)**

* `id`, `reason`, `impactedIds[]`, `risk`, `approvals[]`, `resultingBaselineId`.

**Test**

* `testCase{id, purpose, method, requiredCoverage}`, `testRun{id, env, inputs, results, verdict}`, `coverage{type, pct}`.

**Nonconformance (NCR/CAPA)**

* `id`, `source` (line|field), `severity`, `containment`, `rootCause`, `actions[]`, `closureEvidence`.

**Process**

* `routing`, `operation`, `parameters`, `workInstructionRef`, `capabilityIndices (Cp/Cpk)`.

**Asset**

* `assetId`, `class`, `location`, `capabilities`, `maintHistory[]`, `telemetryBindings`.

**Twin**

* `twinId`, `kind` (product|system|asset|process), `lineage{asBuilt, asMaintained}`, `bindings`, `state`, `kpIs`.

**Document**

* `docId`, `type` (ADR|spec|drawing|evidence), `sourceBindings` (graph queries), `signatures[]`.

> Tip: publish OpenAPI/AsyncAPI & ontology terms for each.

---

# 2) Traceability Graph

**Purpose:** reason over the lifecycle; drive impact analysis, compliance, and ops feedback.

## 2.1 Storage & write pattern

* **Graph DB** (Neo4j/JanusGraph) populated **only** by consuming canonical events (CQRS).
* Graph **schema-on-read** with a **governed ontology** (link types and constraints).
* **Edges are first-class:** they carry `type`, `role`, `createdBy`, `createdAt`, `confidence`, `justification`, and **signatures** when part of a baseline.

## 2.2 Canonical link types (non-exhaustive)

`derivesFrom`, `satisfies`, `implements`, `verifies`, `allocatedTo`, `affectsVariant`, `refines`, `mitigates`, `causes`, `dependsOn`, `asBuiltOf`, `asMaintainedOf`, `produces`, `consumes`.

* Each link type has **domain constraints** (e.g., `verifies: TestCase|TestRun -> Requirement`).
* **SHACL/constraint rules** validate graph integrity (e.g., safety requirements must have ≥1 `verifies` link before release).

## 2.3 Signed snapshots (baselines)

* **What is signed:** node + edge set + selected attributes (whitelist) + digests of attached files/models.
* **How:** topologically sorted serialization → Merkle root → DSSE signature → stored as `Baseline` node with `hash`, `signatures[]`, `policyVersion`.
* **Rebuild:** supply baseline ID → materialize consistent read views and fetch exact doc/model versions.

## 2.4 Queries (examples)

* **Impact:** `MATCH (r:Requirement {id:$id})-[:satisfies|implements|verifies*1..5]->(n) RETURN n` (bounded hops, ranked by change recency).
* **Evidence pack:** declarative template → parameterized graph query set → NLG renderer.
* **Ops linkage:** from `NCR` or `Alarm` to upstream `Part` → `Change` → `Requirement`.

**SLO:** P95 impact traversal for 10k-node neighborhood ≤ **30s**.

---

# 3) Data Contracts & Quality

## 3.1 Contracts

* **Versioned schemas** in a registry (e.g., Confluent): `group: dom.{context}`, `artifact: {Aggregate}{Event}`, `semver`.
* **Compat policy:** backward compatible minor/patch; major for breaking.
* **Change control:** schema PR needs sample payloads, data classification, deprecation plan, consumer impact.

## 3.2 Event envelope (minimal)

```json
{
  "eventId": "ULID",
  "eventType": "ChangeApproved",
  "aggregateId": "eco-55",
  "tenantId": "t-001",
  "occurredAt": "2025-11-04T12:00:00Z",
  "actor": {"id":"u-42","type":"user"},
  "data": {...},
  "schemaVersion": "2.1.0",
  "hash": "sha256-...",
  "classifications": ["confidential"]
}
```

## 3.3 Data quality SLAs

* **Freshness:** projections lag < **60s** P95 from source event.
* **Completeness:** required fields present ≥ **99.5%** by class (e.g., safety requirements).
* **Uniqueness:** collision rate 0 for IDs; dedupe of duplicate imports.
* **Validity:** SHACL/JSON Schema passes ≥ **99.9%**; violations land in quarantine with reasons.
* **Lineage:** 100% artifacts have upstream `createdBy` and event provenance.

**Quality pipeline:** ingest → validate (schema + business) → enrich (units, classification) → publish → monitor dashboards; owners paged on SLO breach.

---

# 4) Twin Hierarchy & Executable Semantics

## 4.1 Hierarchy model

* **Product Twin**: released configuration (BOM + SW + parameters) for a *type*.
* **System Twin**: composition of product twins for a specific system (e.g., a vehicle or line).
* **Asset Twin**: *instance-level* twin of a deployed asset (serial number).
* **Process Twin**: representation of a line/workcell/process incl. routings and capability models.
* **Twin-of-twins**: composition graph; each edge records interface contracts.

**Fields (common):**
`id`, `kind`, `lifecycleState (planned|released|commissioned|operational|retired)`, `lineage{asDesigned, asBuilt, asMaintained}`, `bindings{telemetry[], workInstructions[], tests[]}`, `models{fmu[], cfd[], fea[]}`, `kpis{...}`.

## 4.2 Config lineage

* **asDesigned:** refs to Requirement/Design/BOM baseline.
* **asBuilt:** manufacturing lot/serials, deviations, test results.
* **asMaintained:** service records, parameter drifts, software patches.

**Drift detection:** `diff(asMaintained, asBuilt)` triggers `TwinConfigChanged` events + CAPA suggestions.

## 4.3 Executable semantics (FMI/FMU)

* **Registry:** each twin may attach **FMUs** with `ioContracts`, `units`, `solverSettings`.
* **Orchestration:** Simulation service runs FMUs with scenario parameters; records full **provenance** (toolchain digest, seeds).
* **Virtual commissioning:** process/system twins execute control logic against simulated plant models before go-live.

**Acceptance:** re-running with same inputs yields identical outputs within tolerance; results are linked as `verifies` evidence.

## 4.4 Access control & safety

* Sensitive models flagged; ABAC policies require clearance; watermarking and non-exportable viewer streams for external parties.

---

# 5) Historian Bridge & Time-Series Strategy

## 5.1 Sources

* **SCADA/DCS historians** (e.g., PI, Ignition, DeltaV), **OPC UA** servers, **MQTT Sparkplug B** edge networks.

## 5.2 Ingestion architecture

* **Edge agent** (plant) → Gateway → Kafka ingest topics (`iot.{site}.{asset}.{signal}`)
* **CDC connectors** for classic historians (snapshot + backfill).
* **Transformers** (Flink) perform:

  * **Unit normalization** (UCUM/UDUNITS): store canonical `SI` + original.
  * **Quality flags** (good|bad|uncertain), **status codes**, **operator overrides**.
  * **Late/Out-of-order handling**: watermarking + reorder buffer (configurable per signal).
  * **Compression**: swing-door trending or Gorilla; downsampled rollups (1s/10s/1m/15m/1h) with aggregation functions and **provenance** (method, params).

**Schema (minimal)**

```json
{
  "ts":"2025-11-04T12:00:00.000Z",
  "assetId":"asset-123",
  "signal":"torque",
  "value":54.2,
  "uom":"N·m",
  "value_si":54.2,
  "quality":"good",
  "source":"sparkplug",
  "ingestLagMs": 420
}
```

## 5.3 Storage & indexing

* **Hot**: Timescale/VictoriaMetrics (last 30–90 days) with tags `{tenant, site, asset, signal}`.
* **Warm/Cold**: Iceberg partitioned by `tenant/site/day`; Z-order on `assetId, signal`.
* **Materialized views** for SPC, OEE, alarms, CAPA triggers.

## 5.4 Late data & reconciliation

* Watermarks per stream; **backfill windows** with overwrite-safe merges in Iceberg.
* **Reconciliation job** emits `RecomputedMetric` events when KPIs change due to late data; downstream dashboards update.

## 5.5 Units & calibration

* **Unit dictionary** per signal; conversions trace to standard sources.
* **Calibration records** in Asset Registry adjust readings (store both raw & calibrated).

**SLOs**

* End-to-end ingest latency (edge→hot store) P95 < **10s**.
* Data loss rate < **1e-6** events.
* Late-arrival within configured window absorbed without user-visible errors.

---

# 6) Governance & Stewardship

* **Data Owners** per domain service; **Stewards** per curated dataset (BOMs, twins, tests).
* **Catalog** (Atlas/Amundsen): glossary, ownership, lineage (column/field).
* **Policy-as-code** for retention, residency, classification.
* Quarterly **schema health** reviews (breakage risk, deprecations).
* **PI metrics:** quality SLOs, freshness, consumer adoption, schema change lead time.

---

# 7) KPIs & SLOs (roll-up)

* **Trace completeness:** ≥ **95%** on release baselines.
* **Graph traversal:** impact set P95 ≤ **30s** (10k neighborhood).
* **Data freshness:** search/projections ≤ **60s** P95 lag from source.
* **Twin coverage:** 100% shipped assets registered within 24h of commissioning.
* **Historian ingest:** P95 edge→dash ≤ **10s**; late data reconciliation < **15 min** from arrival.
* **Evidence rebuild:** baseline → pack generation ≤ **2 min** P95.

---

# 8) “Works in real life” Acceptance Tests

1. **Signed trace bundle**

   * Create requirement → link to design & test → baseline → generate hash/sign.
   * **Verify:** rehydrate baseline on fresh environment, links identical, evidence pack matches hash.

2. **Variant-aware impact**

   * Add rule “EU market ⇒ EMC tests”. Change EU requirement.
   * **Verify:** impact graph includes EU-only tests/parts; US variant unaffected.

3. **Twin drift**

   * Commission asset with torque=50 N·m; field updates to 55.
   * **Verify:** `TwinConfigChanged` emitted; CAPA suggestion; work instruction updated; trace shows upstream requirement.

4. **Historian late data**

   * Backfill a day with corrected temperature; SPC shifts.
   * **Verify:** Iceberg merge updates aggregates; `RecomputedMetric` fired; dashboards and any open NCR analysis recomputed.

5. **Schema evolution**

   * Add `confidence` to `verifies` link (minor version).
   * **Verify:** old consumers continue; new consumers read field; registry records compat check; no DLQ growth.
