### 1. Unified design workspace

A web-based or desktop IDE for hardware design, centered on **RTL, hierarchy, connectivity, and design review**.

#### Core editing and navigation

* RTL source editing with syntax highlighting for Verilog, SystemVerilog, VHDL, Chisel, and DSL-generated HDL
* Semantic parsing of hardware code, not just text parsing
* Symbol-aware navigation across modules, interfaces, packages, parameters, and typedefs
* Click-through navigation from instantiations to module definitions
* Jump-to-definition for signals, ports, enums, structs, macros, and parameters
* Find all references for nets, regs, wires, ports, and parameters
* Workspace-wide search across source, constraints, scripts, testbenches, and documentation
* Multi-file editing with tabs, split panes, and pinned files
* Design-aware breadcrumbs showing hierarchical location
* Outline panel for the current module or package
* Code folding for modules, tasks, functions, always blocks, and generate blocks
* Cross-file dependency explorer
* Inline type and width inference display
* Hover tooltips for signal width, direction, ownership, and resolved parameter values
* Diff-aware navigation showing what changed between revisions
* Read-only browsing mode for generated or protected artifacts
* Support for generated sources and source-to-generated traceability
* Per-file metadata panels showing origin, generator, toolchain, and timestamp

#### Module hierarchy and structural exploration

* Hierarchical module browser with expandable tree view
* Instance tree navigation from top-level system down to leaf cells
* Reverse hierarchy search from a signal or module to all parents and consumers
* Instance filtering by module type, clock domain, reset domain, or synthesis group
* Visual hierarchy breadcrumbs with one-click backtracking
* Collapsible subtrees for large SoCs and subsystems
* Hierarchy bookmarks for common entry points
* Structural annotations for wrappers, black boxes, IP blocks, and hard macros
* Differentiation between source hierarchy and elaborated hierarchy
* Elaboration-aware view showing parameterized module instantiations
* Generate-block expansion viewer
* Conditional compilation view for `ifdef`-based design variants
* Configuration-dependent hierarchy overlays
* Compare two hierarchy snapshots side by side
* Show hierarchy size metrics: instance count, signal count, module depth
* Identify hierarchy boundaries for subsystems and ownership domains
* Visual indication of reused IP, vendor blocks, and custom blocks
* Top-down and bottom-up hierarchy traversal modes
* Cross-probing between hierarchy tree and schematic/netlist views

#### Signal tracing and connectivity analysis

* Interactive signal tracing from source to sink
* Fan-in and fan-out traversal for any selected net
* Path highlighting through combinational and sequential logic
* Backward trace from an output to root causes
* Forward trace from an input to all affected downstream logic
* Trace filters by clock domain, hierarchy level, combinational depth, or module type
* Cross-clock signal tracing with CDC annotations
* Reset propagation tracing
* Enable/ready/valid handshake tracing
* Bus transaction tracing from protocol signal bundles
* Named path groups for common interfaces
* Trace collapse/expand controls for cleaner large-fanout paths
* Signal provenance view showing who drives a net and under what conditions
* Multi-driver detection and resolution hints
* Constant propagation trace visibility
* Parameter-dependent connectivity trace resolution
* Trace through generate blocks and conditional logic
* Trace through interface modports and packed structs
* Visual path confidence indicators when some information is inferred
* Trace snapshots saved as shareable artifacts
* Annotated traces with comments and review notes
* Correlated trace to waveform locations and simulation timestamps
* Compare signal traces across design revisions
* Trace diff showing changed drivers, loads, or logic cones
* Highlight illegal or suspicious paths, such as combinational loops
* Search by signal behavior class, not only by name
* Cross-probe trace results back to RTL and netlist views

#### Netlist visualization

* Graph view of elaborated netlist
* RTL-to-netlist projection with source mapping
* Hierarchical schematic view
* Flat connectivity view for local cones
* Instance graph with nodes, pins, and edges
* Zoomable and pannable large graph rendering
* Clustered visualization for large designs
* Collapse by module, interface, or hierarchy boundary
* Expand selected cone to inspect detail
* Cone-of-influence visualization
* Critical-path highlighting
* Timing-path overlay from timing analysis
* Clock-domain coloring
* Reset-domain coloring
* Control/data path distinction
* Bus bundling to reduce clutter
* Edge routing optimization to minimize crossings
* Pin grouping and bus lane alignment
* Search within graph by module, port, or net name
* Graph bookmarks for saved viewpoints
* Path highlighting on click
* Two-node shortest path discovery
* Multi-hop transitive fanout exploration
* Shared subgraph detection
* Duplicate structure detection for repeated pipelines or replicated datapaths
* Pattern matching for common structures like FIFOs, arbiters, mux trees, or pipelines
* Schematic export to image/PDF/SVG
* Graph layout algorithms for hierarchy-preserving and flat layouts
* Filter by signal class: control, data, clock, reset, debug, handshake
* Overlay of assertions, coverage points, and simulation hotspots
* Overlay of power/toggle information
* Overlay of timing slack and violation markers
* View synthesized netlist versus pre-synthesis RTL netlist
* Technology-mapped gate-level visualization
* Black-box cell handling with boundary stubs
* Vendor primitive rendering support
* Netlist comparison across revisions or configurations
* Side-by-side graph diff for structural changes
* Search-by-pattern across graphs to find repeated logic structures
* “Explain this logic” assistant panel showing connectivity summary
* Export of subgraphs for documentation and review

#### Schema, parameters, and configuration management

* Centralized parameter browser for all modules and configurations
* Parameter inheritance and override tracing
* Default-value resolution with origin tracking
* Parameter validation rules and constraint checking
* Parameter dependency graph
* Compile-time versus runtime parameter separation
* Generated configuration manifest viewing
* Typed parameter editing with schema enforcement
* Numeric, enum, boolean, string, struct, and list parameter support
* Range constraints and allowed-value sets
* Derived parameter visualization
* Environment-specific configuration overlays
* Design variant matrix for comparing configurations
* Parameter diff between two builds
* “What changed?” view when a parameter impacts multiple modules
* Configuration lock and freeze states for release builds
* Parameter templates for common architecture families
* Import/export of parameter sets as JSON, YAML, TOML, or domain-specific config
* Configuration versioning with audit history
* Search by parameter name, value, dependency, or impacted module
* Validation warnings for incompatible combinations
* Elaboration preview before committing configuration changes
* Configuration simulations to see resulting hierarchy and resource impact
* Constraint attachment to parameters, such as timing, area, or power limits
* Parameter provenance showing where each value originated
* Environment variable and secret integration for sensitive build inputs
* Cross-referencing between config, source code, and generated artifacts
* Variant comparison view across families of chips
* Batch editing of related parameters
* Parameter preset library for reusable designs
* Snapshotting of design configuration for reproducible experiments

#### Hardware code review

* Code review interface specialized for RTL and hardware collateral
* Hierarchy-aware diff views, not only line-based diffs
* Signal-aware diffs that understand renames, moves, and elaboration changes
* Semantic diffs for changed logic behavior
* Module-level and file-level review modes
* Review comments on modules, ports, signals, instances, and net connections
* Inline comments on specific always blocks, generate blocks, or case items
* Comment threads linked to design objects, not just file lines
* Review states: draft, under review, approved, rejected, superseded
* Ownership assignment for review areas
* Review checklist templates for hardware signoff
* Review labels for functional, timing, CDC, DFT, lint, and style concerns
* Impact analysis panel showing affected hierarchy and dependent modules
* Auto-generated review summary from structural diffs
* Side-by-side compare for RTL, synthesized netlists, and generated docs
* Artifact diff for constraints, scripts, manifests, and testbench updates
* Change risk scoring based on fanout, timing impact, or critical path proximity
* Review gating by assertions, coverage, or verification status
* “Needs re-elaboration” and “needs resynthesis” markers
* Review history and approval audit trail
* Suggested reviewers based on module ownership and dependency graph
* Batch approval for low-risk generated changes
* Reviewable snapshots tied to simulation results
* Merge request integration for Git-based workflows
* Change request linking to bugs, requirements, and verification items
* Review reminders and stale review detection
* Comment resolution workflows with evidence attachments
* Hardware-specific blame/annotate support with hierarchy context

#### Collaboration and shared workspace

* Multi-user live collaboration in the same design session
* Presence indicators showing who is inspecting which block
* Shared cursors and annotations
* Threaded discussion attached to design objects
* @mentions for module owners or reviewers
* Shared bookmarks and saved views
* Team dashboards for subsystem ownership
* Permission controls by project, module, and artifact type
* Read-only and edit roles
* Locked blocks for signoff or release
* History timeline for design changes
* Replay of design edits and review events
* Shared design “tour” mode for walkthroughs
* Linkable deep URLs to modules, signals, traces, and graph states
* Exportable review packets for offline discussion
* Workspace activity feeds
* Notifications for changes to watched signals or modules
* Audit logs for all edits and approvals

#### Productivity and ergonomics

* Command palette for all major actions
* Keyboard-first navigation across the platform
* Customizable shortcuts for hardware engineers
* Multiple themes optimized for dense RTL code
* High-DPI rendering for complex diagrams
* Minimal and distraction-free coding mode
* Dockable panels for hierarchy, trace, graph, and review tools
* Saved workspace layouts
* Session restore after browser or app restart
* Multi-monitor support
* Offline/local editing with later sync
* Autosave and version recovery
* Smart opening of related files and views
* Context-sensitive quick actions
* Inline generation of boilerplate for modules, interfaces, and test stubs
* Snippets for common HDL patterns
* Template library for design blocks
* Search and replace with semantic awareness
* Refactoring helpers for renaming signals, modules, and parameters
* Safe rename propagation across hierarchy and references
* Duplicate code detection for repeated RTL patterns
* Lint suggestions embedded in the editor
* Structural warnings in the gutter and minimap
* Error navigation with one-click next/previous issue
* Deep integration with terminal, build logs, and simulator output
* Unified tabs for source, waveform, graph, and report views

#### Import/export and interoperability

* Import existing RTL projects from Git repositories
* Import elaborated netlists from common tool outputs
* Import third-party IP metadata
* Import constraints and build scripts
* Export design views as PDF, SVG, PNG, or HTML
* Export module documentation pages
* Export annotated design reviews
* Export configuration manifests
* Export trace reports and dependency graphs
* Export synthesis-ready or simulation-ready bundles
* Interoperability with external HDL parsers and linters
* Adapter support for commercial and open-source EDA tools
* API access for automation and scripting
* Batch operations from CLI or CI pipelines

#### Intelligence and automation

* Auto-elaboration previews before build
* Suggest likely drivers and sinks for unlabeled nets
* Detect probable clock/reset nets automatically
* Identify handshake protocols and interface bundles
* Infer module roles such as FIFO, arbiter, ALU, or register file
* Detect repeated structural motifs across the design
* Suggest hierarchy normalization opportunities
* Highlight unused ports, nets, and parameters
* Surface combinational loops, latch inference, and width mismatches
* Auto-summarize module purpose from structure and comments
* Generate documentation drafts from the live design
* Recommend missing assertions based on module behavior
* Recommend regression targets based on affected hierarchy
* Identify risky edits before commit
* Suggest refactorings to reduce fanout, depth, or complexity
* Offer design-space alternatives for selected blocks
* Smart bookmarks for commonly inspected signals and modules

#### Documentation and knowledge capture

* Auto-generated module documentation pages
* Signal dictionaries and interface catalogs
* Architecture notes linked to implementation
* Review decision logs
* Design rationale tracking
* Block diagrams with synchronized source links
* Living specification pages for each subsystem
* Markdown, AsciiDoc, and rich-text notes embedded in workspace
* Requirement traceability links
* Glossary of terms and protocol definitions
* Design ownership directory
* Change log per module and per release
* “How it works” autogenerated overviews for newcomers
* Captured review outcomes and engineering decisions
* Searchable design wiki integrated with artifacts

#### Quality and governance

* Lint integration for RTL style and consistency
* CDC-aware warnings surfaced in context
* Reset-domain warnings surfaced in context
* Parameter validity gates
* Naming convention enforcement
* Module boundary rule enforcement
* Hierarchy depth limits and exceptions
* Signoff readiness indicators
* Block readiness state machine
* Policy-driven approval flows
* Compliance checks for forbidden primitives or constructs
* Artifact provenance and reproducibility metadata
* Immutable release snapshots
* Signed build manifests
* Traceable approval trails
* Role-based access control
* Secret handling for secure design data
* Artifact retention rules and archival policies



The key idea is that a design is not just source code; it is a **system graph**.

### 2. Architecture sandbox

A place to model, simulate, compare, and iterate on processor and system architectures across the full design space.

#### Architecture definition and modeling

* Define architectures as first-class objects, not ad hoc text files
* Create named architecture families with inheritance and specialization
* Model complete systems, subsystems, cores, clusters, and accelerators
* Describe architectures declaratively, imperatively, or via a GUI
* Support parameterized architecture templates
* Support partial architecture definitions with defaults and overrides
* Version architecture definitions independently from RTL
* Attach metadata to each architecture, including intent, assumptions, and target market
* Model abstract, detailed, and mixed-fidelity components
* Represent architecture as a directed graph of functional blocks
* Express component composition hierarchically or flat
* Model compute, memory, interconnect, and control planes separately
* Support architecture descriptors for CPUs, DSPs, GPUs, NPUs, and domain-specific accelerators
* Model embedded, server, edge, and real-time configurations
* Model heterogeneous systems with multiple core types
* Support architecture constraints, such as area, power, latency, and frequency targets
* Support architecture “profiles” for different workload classes
* Support design intent tags such as performance-first, power-first, area-first, or balanced
* Allow architecture annotations for research notes and tradeoff hypotheses

#### In-order core modeling

* Specify pipeline depth and stage boundaries
* Configure fetch, decode, execute, memory, and writeback stages
* Model single-issue and multi-issue in-order pipelines
* Model stall propagation and bubble insertion
* Model bypass and forwarding paths
* Model hazard detection logic
* Model structural, data, and control hazards
* Model register file ports and access contention
* Model instruction fetch width and decode bandwidth
* Model branch penalty behavior
* Model load-use latency
* Model memory ordering behavior
* Model exceptions and interrupt entry/exit behavior
* Model simple scoreboarding for in-order issue
* Support pipeline flushing policies
* Support pipeline drain behavior for traps and interrupts
* Support microarchitectural counters for stalls and hazards

#### Out-of-order core modeling

* Model reservation stations and issue queues
* Model reorder buffer capacity and commit behavior
* Model register renaming and physical register files
* Model free list and rename table policies
* Model speculative execution windows
* Model load/store queues and memory disambiguation
* Model wakeup/select mechanisms
* Model dispatch, issue, execute, and retire widths independently
* Model branch misprediction recovery and rollback
* Model reorder buffer checkpointing
* Model precise exception support
* Model memory ordering fences and speculation barriers
* Model speculation depth and recovery latency
* Model execution port allocation and contention
* Model functional unit latencies and throughputs
* Model clustered execution units
* Model multi-domain out-of-order designs with shared frontend/backend options
* Model SMT-like sharing policies if needed
* Model commit bandwidth bottlenecks
* Model instruction fusion and macro-op expansion

#### Superscalar pipeline modeling

* Configure issue width, fetch width, and retire width independently
* Model instruction pairing rules
* Model decode bottlenecks and front-end saturation
* Model multiple execution lanes
* Model vector and scalar execution sharing
* Model structural hazards across shared resources
* Model rename and dispatch pressure
* Model branch predictor bandwidth interactions
* Model instruction cache and decode queue buffering
* Model replay mechanisms for load misses and execution conflicts
* Model pipeline stage balancing
* Model micro-op cache effects
* Model frontend/backend decoupling
* Model throughput under mixed instruction mixes
* Analyze width scaling efficiency
* Compare narrow-deep versus wide-shallow tradeoffs

#### Cache hierarchy modeling

* Model L1 instruction cache and data cache separately
* Model unified versus split caches
* Model L2 private caches and shared caches
* Model L3 and LLC configurations
* Model cache size, associativity, line size, and replacement policy
* Model write-through and write-back policies
* Model allocate-on-write and no-write-allocate behaviors
* Model victim caches
* Model cache inclusivity and exclusivity
* Model cache banking and multi-ported access
* Model prefetcher policies
* Model cache coherence directory storage
* Model cache way prediction
* Model cache slicing and cluster-local caches
* Model cache compression and metadata overhead
* Model cache access latency by level and topology
* Model cache miss handling with MSHRs
* Model hit-under-miss and miss-under-miss behavior
* Model bandwidth constraints and backpressure
* Model warm-up and cold-start effects
* Model cache pollution and thrashing scenarios
* Model software-controlled caching policies
* Model scratchpad versus cache tradeoffs

#### Coherence and memory consistency modeling

* Model MESI, MOESI, MSI, and custom protocols
* Model snooping and directory-based coherence
* Model inclusive, non-inclusive, and exclusive coherence topologies
* Model coherence message traffic
* Model invalidation versus update-based protocols
* Model sharer tracking and directory scaling
* Model cache-to-cache transfers
* Model coherence point latency
* Model write serialization behavior
* Model memory consistency models such as SC, TSO, and weaker models
* Model fence costs and ordering constraints
* Model atomic operations and lock primitives
* Model cache line state transitions
* Model false sharing behavior
* Model coherence hotspots and traffic hotspots
* Model NUMA effects in multi-chip or multi-die systems
* Model remote memory access penalties
* Model coherence debugging visualizations
* Compare coherence protocol overhead across workloads

#### Branch prediction modeling

* Model static and dynamic branch predictors
* Model bimodal, gshare, tournament, and perceptron predictors

* Model branch target prediction accuracy
* Model return address stack behavior
* Model indirect branch prediction
* Model loop predictors
* Model hybrid predictor designs
* Model history length tuning

#### NoC and interconnect modeling

* Model mesh, torus, tree, ring, and crossbar topologies
* Model hierarchical NoC designs

* Model wormhole, store-and-forward, and virtual cut-through routing

* Model memory traffic over NoC

* Visualize flits, packets, and congestion hotspots
* Compare topology cost/performance tradeoffs

#### Memory controller modeling

* Model single-channel and multi-channel controllers
* Model DDR, LPDDR, HBM, and custom memory interfaces

* Model scheduling policies such as FCFS, FR-FCFS, and QoS-aware schedulers

* Model read/write turnaround penalties

* Model coprocessor attachment points

* Model DMA engine integration
* Model shared-memory accelerator access

* Model interrupt-driven versus polling-driven accelerator control
* Compare insertion point impact on critical path and timing closure

#### Design-space exploration

* Sweep architecture parameters automatically
* Generate architecture variants from a parameter grid
* Generate variants from heuristic search
* Support random search, greedy search, and evolutionary search
* Support Bayesian optimization for architecture tuning

This sandbox would become the place where you stop arguing abstractly about “better cores” and start proving it quantitatively.


### 3. Simulation engine

This is the heart of the platform.

A simulation subsystem for running architectural, microarchitectural, RTL-adjacent, and system-level models with multiple fidelity modes, time control, state inspection, and variant comparison.

#### Simulation kernel and execution model

* Core simulation kernel as a first-class platform service
* Deterministic execution mode for reproducible runs
* Non-deterministic execution mode for randomized stress testing
* Single-threaded simulation mode for debugging
* Multi-threaded simulation mode for throughput
* Distributed simulation mode for large systems
* Incremental simulation for small design changes
* Checkpointable execution state
* Serializable simulator state for pause/resume
* Reproducible seed management
* Simulation clock abstraction
* Support for discrete-event semantics
* Support for cycle-based semantics
* Support for hybrid event/cycle execution
* Temporal ordering guarantees
* Priority-based event scheduling
* Zero-delay event handling
* Delta-cycle processing
* Stable ordering for simultaneous events
* Time resolution configuration
* Time unit conversion and normalization
* Wall-clock to simulated-time mapping
* Simulation lifecycle hooks
* Start, pause, resume, stop, and reset operations
* Per-run metadata capture
* Run provenance tracking
* Simulation run isolation
* Headless batch execution
* Interactive execution sessions
* Embedded execution inside IDE workflows
* API-driven execution for automation

#### Cycle-accurate simulation

* Cycle-accurate modeling for critical microarchitectural blocks

* Accurate stage occupancy tracking
* Fetch/decode/rename/dispatch/issue/execute/commit timing

* Load/store timing
* Cache access timing
* Memory latency propagation
* Backpressure modeling

### 4. Hardware/software co-design layer

This is the layer that turns the platform from a chip modeling tool into a **full-stack co-design environment**. Hardware and software are treated as one system with shared contracts, shared artifacts, shared versioning, and shared validation.

#### Co-design domain model

* Define hardware/software boundaries as explicit first-class artifacts

* Link every software artifact back to the hardware object it controls

### 5. Configurable chip generator

For software-defined chips, this is the subsystem that turns architecture intent into **concrete chip variants**. It should accept a rich parameter model, resolve dependencies, elaborate the design, and emit a complete bundle of implementation and verification artifacts.

#### Parameter model and configuration definition

* Define chips as parameterized families rather than single fixed designs
* Support top-level chip templates with inheritance and specialization

* Support locked parameters that cannot be changed downstream
* Support derived parameters computed from other parameters
* Support conditional parameters that appear only when certain features are enabled
* Support mutually exclusive option groups
* Support required parameter validation
* Support parameter aliasing for backward compatibility
* Support human-readable and machine-readable parameter names
* Support named configuration profiles such as dev, perf, low-power, secure, and debug
* Support target-specific presets for embedded, client, server, edge, and accelerator-heavy chips
* Support parameter namespaces to avoid collisions across subsystems
* Support versioned configuration schemas
* Support configuration annotations explaining intent and tradeoffs
* Support frozen snapshots for reproducible chip builds
* Support configuration inheritance across chip generations
* Support override chains from product line to SKU to build
* Support parameter provenance tracking
* Support invalid combination detection before elaboration
* Support semantic validation beyond simple type checking
* Support configuration diffs and merge workflows
* Support config migration when schemas evolve
* Support config templates for common architecture families
* Support programmatic and GUI-based configuration editing
* Support config import/export in JSON, YAML, TOML, and domain-specific formats
* Support environment-specific overlays for simulation, emulation, FPGA, and ASIC flows

### 6. Verification and validation suite

No serious platform survives without this.

This subsystem is the **quality gate** for the entire chip platform: it validates RTL, architecture models, generators, interfaces, software contracts, and end-to-end behavior. It should support correctness, coverage, regression discipline, root-cause analysis, and proof-oriented methods.

#### Verification strategy and scope

* Treat verification as a first-class product area, not a side tool
* Support verification at module, subsystem, chip, and platform levels
* Support pre-silicon, post-synthesis, and post-layout validation workflows
* Support RTL validation, microarchitecture validation, and software-visible behavior validation
* Support functional correctness, timing-related sanity checks, protocol compliance, and performance regressions
* Support simulation-based, property-based, and formal-style verification workflows
* Support verification planning for each design object
* Link each feature to its required tests and proofs
* Maintain verification status per block and per release
* Distinguish between smoke tests, daily regressions, signoff suites, and debug-only suites
* Track signoff criteria explicitly
* Support verification gates in CI, release, and merge workflows
* Support design-stage-specific verification maturity levels
* Support variant-specific verification requirements for configurable chips
* Support traceability from requirement to test to result to signoff

#### Module-level unit test support

* Unit tests for individual RTL modules
* Unit tests for architecture models
* Unit tests for parameter resolvers and generators
* Unit tests for register maps and schema validators
* Unit tests for queue behavior, FIFOs, arbiters, and protocol endpoints
* Unit tests for helper libraries and model primitives
* Module-level test harness generation
* Test fixture generation for modules with dependencies
* Mocking of neighboring modules and external interfaces
* Stubs for clocks, resets, interrupts, and memory responses
* Support for deterministic setup and teardown
* Support for isolated module testing without full chip context
* Support for assertions inside module test environments
* Support for expected failure and edge-case tests
* Support for boundary value testing
* Support for invalid-input and negative tests
* Support for stateful tests across multiple cycles or events
* Support for test parameterization and reuse
* Support for reusable test vectors
* Support for golden reference comparisons
* Support for snapshot-based module tests
* Support for fast micro-tests in developer inner loops

This suite would be the platform’s immune system: it catches design regressions, exposes blind spots, and turns correctness into something measurable and operational.
